<div id="review_1191365783" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1191365783" />
    <a title="Dragana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5084213-dragana"><img alt="Dragana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516620361p2/5084213.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1191365783?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dragana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dragana" href="/user/show/5084213-dragana">Dragana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5084213-dragana?shelf=complex-worlbuilding">complex-worlbuilding</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5084213-dragana?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5084213-dragana?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5084213-dragana?shelf=robots">robots</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5084213-dragana?shelf=geeks-rule">geeks-rule</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1191365783" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18085951473810449451">Its been a while since book left me with so many mixed feelings like Seveneves did.<br/><br/><b>LIKES</b><br/><br/> * <b>Builds on existing technology</b>. Science fiction novels that use current state of our world as a starting point (or existing science concepts) and then build on it are my favorite kind. For example think of anything by Arthur C. Clarke. In Seveneves, everything scientists and engineers do, sounds realizable.<br/><br/> * <b>Made me care</b>. As a speculative fiction fan, I read a lot of apocalyptic and post-apocalyptic books.</span>
  <span id="freeText18085951473810449451" style="display:none">Its been a while since book left me with so many mixed feelings like Seveneves did.<br /><br /><b>LIKES</b><br /><br /> * <b>Builds on existing technology</b>. Science fiction novels that use current state of our world as a starting point (or existing science concepts) and then build on it are my favorite kind. For example think of anything by Arthur C. Clarke. In Seveneves, everything scientists and engineers do, sounds realizable.<br /><br /> * <b>Made me care</b>. As a speculative fiction fan, I read a lot of apocalyptic and post-apocalyptic books. In most of them the big part of the human race dies or has died. But Neal Stephenson really made me care and cheer for the survival of Earth.<br /><br /> * <b>Nerdgasm galore</b>. Neal Stephenson used a lot of interesting science facts as plot elements. I loved all the talk about development of artificial intelligence in robots, genetic engineering and what happens when you do ordinary tasks in space.<br /><br /> * <b>Russians</b>. Serbs and Russians have a shared ancestry and I noticed similarities in mentality and the general way of thinking that always make me smile. While Americans care about safety and take all necessary precautions, Russian technology is straightforward and a bit crazy in it’s simplicity.<br /><br /><i>"The qualifications for being a Scout seemed to be a shocking level of physical endurance, a complete disregard for mortal danger, and some knowledge of how to exist in a space suit. All of them were Russian."</i><br /><br /><b>MIXED FEELINGS</b><br /><br /> * <b>Gut-wrenchingly sad</b>. Remember that part that Neal Stephenson made me care? Well, there is a downside. There are a lot of times when sacrifices had to be made or accidents happened. As a result, a lot of people and even some of the main characters die. While I was reading Seveneves, I had a big knot in my throat. It was all so tragic… I can not say this is bad, but I do not like books that make me sad.<br /><br /> * <b>Annoying characters</b> which I wanted to kill with my bare hands. Arhg! I hated them so much. They exploit and manipulate the others for their own interest. And the worst part, since their highest concern is saving their own ass, is that they usually survive. While good, noble characters die because they make willing sacrifices for the benefit of the human race.<br /><br /><b>DISLIKES</b><br /><br /> * <b>Bored by some scientific information</b>. I liked some of the geeky stuff and Neal Stephenson’s attention to detail, but sometimes he just didn’t know when to stop and went into too much detail. It might be my fault, since some topics were not as interesting to me as others. For example: when the explanations about the propulsion, directions and amount needed to move a vehicles in space would start, I would just space out and skim until he changed the topics.<br /><br /> * <b>Big paragraphs</b>, sometimes spanning a couple of pages. I felt smothered with so much descriptions, all thrown at me without any break.<br /><br /> * <b>Meh ending</b>. After apocalypse and 5000 years I didn’t get the impression that human race improved at all. They still make the same mistakes. Why the hell did I read 880 pages for? Give me some hope!<br /><br /><b>IN THE END…</b><br /><br />Seveneves is a book that leaves me with a lot of thoughts and topics for discussion. I wish I read it in some book club, so we could chat about interesting geeky details, favorite emotional moments and rant about the characters we hate.<br /><br />When it comes to recommending Seveneves, I am not sure what to say. I think big space geeks will enjoy so many details about living in space, space mechanics and other data. If you have that one friend who spams you with movies like <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P36xhtpw0Lg" rel="nofollow noopener">Tears in Space (Don’t Fall)</a> recommend Seveneves to him.<br /><br /><i><b>Disclaimer:</b> I received this ebook from Edelweiss in exchange for a fair and honest review. This text is also posted on <a href="http://www.bookwormdreams.com/book-review-seveneves-by-neal-stephenson/" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog Bookworm Dreams</a> in a little bit more styled edition.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="18085951473810449451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1129691118" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1129691118" />
    <a title="Liviu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1229019-liviu"><img alt="Liviu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389592122p2/1229019.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1129691118?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liviu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liviu" href="/user/show/1229019-liviu">Liviu</a>
      </span>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1129691118" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8856980089389432484">The most expected sf novel of the year for me turned out to be quite frustrating as it clearly could have been awesome and among the best sf of all time if it just started on page 516 or so with what was advertised in the blurb (the seven races terraforming the earth etc); but for 500+ pages the book is a competent mixture of techno-thriller apocalyptic/post apocalyptic sf with some very unrealistic assumptions (something like the hard rain of the novel coming up would induce massive breakdown o</span>
  <span id="freeText8856980089389432484" style="display:none">The most expected sf novel of the year for me turned out to be quite frustrating as it clearly could have been awesome and among the best sf of all time if it just started on page 516 or so with what was advertised in the blurb (the seven races terraforming the earth etc); but for 500+ pages the book is a competent mixture of techno-thriller apocalyptic/post apocalyptic sf with some very unrealistic assumptions (something like the hard rain of the novel coming up would induce massive breakdown of the order and a scramble of anyone who is rich and connected for the exits not what is presented in the novel), but with lots of interesting stuff too; however this is stuff that has been overdone and in which i lack that much of an interest - overall a 2 star for those 500+ pages<br /><br />however the last 200 pages - despite the necessary denseness and info dumping which caused many narrative walls for a long while though the last 50 pages or so are superb as narrative too - delivered so much to make the novel quite memorable but also to cause the regret and frustration that not the whole of the 700 pages (or at least the vast majority) were dedicated to them with the hard rain stuff and all the contemporary action relegated to a short prologue and the meeting of the seven eves (well eight, sort of) on page 50 or at most 100...<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8856980089389432484" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vsW9GlF8ZiDYderNyLxlAhzCdjzj9PbHcTvJwdSukZGVD0BYM8vTU6thZU4PnifG6GuDQML0zADqJtzLrIeK6w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QeOyjocTdPTo6D6SOarJIjsUXFFsA9No30wBLlm7sWJqKU/M5aTBh5v8sRH+iIvmz72pLU0D6a9EURQkIZKqGA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15936910221759364090">Neal Stephenson is the author of <i>Reamde, Anathem,</i> and the three-volume historical epic the Baroque Cycle (<i>Quicksilver, The Confusion,</i> and <i>The System of the World</i>), as well as <i>Cryptonomicon, The Diamond Age, Snow Crash,</i> and <i>Zodiac.</i> He lives in Seattle, Washington.</span>
